The Gray code nature is useful (compared to [chain codes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chain_code "Chain code"), also called [De Bruijn sequences](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/De_Bruijn_sequence "De Bruijn sequence")), as only one sensor will change at any one time, so the uncertainty during a transition between two discrete states will only be plus or minus one unit of angular measurement the device is capable of resolving.<sup id="cite_ref-Alciatore-Histand_1999_83-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Alciatore-Histand_1999-83">[81]</a></sup>

### Two-dimensional Gray code\[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Gray_code&action=edit&section=26 "Edit section: Two-dimensional Gray code")\]

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/16QAM_Gray_Coded.svg/200px-16QAM_Gray_Coded.svg.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:16QAM_Gray_Coded.svg)

A Gray-coded constellation diagram for rectangular 16-[QAM](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quadrature_amplitude_modulation "Quadrature amplitude modulation")

Two-dimensional Gray codes are used in communication to minimize the number of bit errors in [quadrature amplitude modulation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quadrature_amplitude_modulation "Quadrature amplitude modulation") (QAM) adjacent points in the [constellation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constellation_diagram "Constellation diagram"). In a typical encoding the horizontal and vertical adjacent constellation points differ by a single bit, and diagonal adjacent points differ by 2 bits.<sup id="cite_ref-Krishna_2008_84-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Krishna_2008-84">[82]</a></sup>

Two-dimensional Gray codes also have uses in [location identifications](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Location_identification "Location identification") schemes, where the code would be applied to area maps such as a [Mercator projection](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mercator_projection "Mercator projection") of the earth's surface and an appropriate cyclic two-dimensional distance function such as the [Mannheim metric](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mannheim_metric "Mannheim metric") be used to calculate the distance between two encoded locations, thereby combining the characteristics of the [Hamming distance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hamming_distance "Hamming distance") with the cyclic continuation of a Mercator projection.<sup id="cite_ref-Strang-Dammann-Roeckl-Plass_2009_85-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Strang-Dammann-Roeckl-Plass_2009-85">[83]</a></sup>

### Excess-Gray-Code\[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Gray_code&action=edit&section=27 "Edit section: Excess-Gray-Code")\]

If a subsection of a specific codevalue is extracted from that value, for example the last 3 bits of a 4-bit gray-code, the resulting code will be an "excess gray code". This code shows the property of counting backwards in those extracted bits if the original value is further increased. Reason for this is that gray-encoded values do not show the behaviour of overflow, known from classic binary encoding, when increasing past the "highest" value.

Example: The highest 3-bit gray code, 7, is encoded as (0)100. Adding 1 results in number 8, encoded in gray as 1100. The last 3 bits do not overflow and count backwards if you further increase the original 4 bit code.

When working with sensors that output multiple, gray-encoded values in a serial fashion, one should therefore pay attention whether the sensor produces those multiple values encoded in 1 single gray-code or as separate ones, as otherwise the values might appear to be counting backwards when an "overflow" is expected.

## Gray isometry\[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Gray_code&action=edit&section=28 "Edit section: Gray isometry")\]

The bijective mapping { 0 ↔ 00, 1 ↔ 01, 2 ↔ 11, 3 ↔ 10 } establishes an [isometry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Isometry "Isometry") between the [metric space](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Metric_space "Metric space") over the [finite field](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Finite_field "Finite field") ![\mathbb {Z} _{2}^{2}](https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f86cdebd065ce715185fea5e604557ac15453826) with the metric given by the [Hamming distance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hamming_distance "Hamming distance") and the metric space over the [finite ring](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Finite_ring "Finite ring") ![\mathbb {Z} _{4}](https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/5ecbc000fbd9a59f44ec7502f5e4f4b24f9a8e06) (the usual [modular arithmetic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Modular_arithmetic "Modular arithmetic")) with the metric given by the [Lee distance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lee_distance "Lee distance"). The mapping is suitably extended to an isometry of the [Hamming spaces](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hamming_space "Hamming space") ![\mathbb {Z} _{2}^{2m}](https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/c95e46f6e851988f7bf14fed668b93831351f148) and ![\mathbb {Z} _{4}^{m}](https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/17ffb5c4a91673878356885f5d3401856c907eef). Its importance lies in establishing a correspondence between various "good" but not necessarily [linear codes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Linear_code "Linear code") as Gray-map images in ![\mathbb {Z} _{2}^{2}](https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f86cdebd065ce715185fea5e604557ac15453826) of [ring-linear codes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Linear_code#Generalization "Linear code") from ![\mathbb {Z} _{4}](https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/5ecbc000fbd9a59f44ec7502f5e4f4b24f9a8e06).<sup id="cite_ref-Greferath_2009_86-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Greferath_2009-86">[84]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Hazewinkel-Sole_2016_87-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Hazewinkel-Sole_2016-87">[85]</a></sup>

## \[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Gray_code&action=edit&section=29 "Edit section: Related codes")\]

There are a number of binary codes similar to Gray codes, including:

-   Datex codes aka Giannini codes (1954), as described by Carl P. Spaulding,<sup id="cite_ref-Spaulding_1954_8-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Spaulding_1954-8">[8]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Spaulding_1965_88-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Spaulding_1965-88">[86]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Wheeler_1969_89-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Wheeler_1969-89">[87]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Dokter-Steinhauer_1973_90-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Dokter-Steinhauer_1973-90">[88]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Dokter-Steinhauer_1975_91-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Dokter-Steinhauer_1975-91">[89]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MIL_1991_7-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-MIL_1991-7">[7]</a></sup> use a variant of [O'Brien code II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#O'Brien_II).
-   Codes used by Varec (ca. 1954),<sup id="cite_ref-Varec_1954_92-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Varec_1954-92">[90]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Bishup-Repeta-Giarrizzo_1963_93-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Bishup-Repeta-Giarrizzo_1963-93">[91]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Whessoe_1993_94-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Whessoe_1993-94">[92]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Emerson_95-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Emerson-95">[93]</a></sup> use a variant of [O'Brien code I](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#O'Brien_I) as well as base-12 and base-16 Gray code variants.
-   Lucal code (1959)<sup id="cite_ref-Lucal_1959_1-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Lucal_1959-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sellers-Hsiao-Bearnson_1968_2-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Sellers-Hsiao-Bearnson_1968-2">[2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Doran_2007_57-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Doran_2007-57">[56]</a></sup> aka modified reflected binary code (MRB)<sup id="cite_ref-Lucal_1959_1-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Lucal_1959-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sellers-Hsiao-Bearnson_1968_2-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Sellers-Hsiao-Bearnson_1968-2">[2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NB_Modified_96-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-NB_Modified-96">[nb 3]</a></sup>
-   [Gillham code](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gillham_code "Gillham code") (1961/1962),<sup id="cite_ref-Wheeler_1969_89-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Wheeler_1969-89">[87]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Wightman_1972_97-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Wightman_1972-97">[94]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MIL_1991_7-3"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-MIL_1991-7">[7]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Phillips_1998_98-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Phillips_1998-98">[95]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Stewart_2010_99-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Stewart_2010-99">[96]</a></sup> uses a variant of [Datex](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#Datex) code and [O'Brien code II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#O'Brien_II).
-   Leslie and Russell code (1964)<sup id="cite_ref-Leslie-Russell_1964_100-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Leslie-Russell_1964-100">[97]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Russell_1964_9-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Russell_1964-9">[9]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Leslie_1974_101-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Leslie_1974-101">[98]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Wightman_1972_97-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Wightman_1972-97">[94]</a></sup>
-   Royal Radar Establishment code<sup id="cite_ref-Wightman_1972_97-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Wightman_1972-97">[94]</a></sup>
-   Hoklas code (1988)<sup id="cite_ref-Hoklas_1989_102-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Hoklas_1989-102">[99]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Hoklas_2005_1_103-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Hoklas_2005_1-103">[100]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Hoklas_2005_2_104-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Hoklas_2005_2-104">[101]</a></sup>

The following [binary-coded decimal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Binary-coded_decimal "Binary-coded decimal") (BCD) codes are Gray code variants as well:

-   Petherick code (1953),<sup id="cite_ref-Petherick_1953_18-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Petherick_1953-18">[18]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Petherick-Hopkins_1958_105-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Petherick-Hopkins_1958-105">[102]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Baumgartner_1963_106-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Baumgartner_1963-106">[103]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Charnley-Bidgood-Boardman_1965_107-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Charnley-Bidgood-Boardman_1965-107">[104]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Powell_1968_55-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Powell_1968-55">[54]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Hoklas_2005_1_103-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Hoklas_2005_1-103">[100]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NB_Petherick_OBrien-II_108-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-NB_Petherick_OBrien-II-108">[nb 4]</a></sup> also known as [Royal Aircraft Establishment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Royal_Aircraft_Establishment "Royal Aircraft Establishment") (RAE) code.<sup id="cite_ref-Hollingdale_1958_109-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Hollingdale_1958-109">[105]</a></sup>
-   O'Brien codes I and II (1955)<sup id="cite_ref-O'Brien_1955_110-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-O'Brien_1955-110">[106]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Steinbuch_1962_111-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Steinbuch_1962-111">[107]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Steinbuch-Weber-Heinemann_1974_112-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Steinbuch-Weber-Heinemann_1974-112">[108]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Dokter-Steinhauer_1973_90-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Dokter-Steinhauer_1973-90">[88]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Dokter-Steinhauer_1975_91-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Dokter-Steinhauer_1975-91">[89]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Hoklas_2005_1_103-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Hoklas_2005_1-103">[100]</a></sup> (An O'Brien type-I code<sup id="cite_ref-NB_OBrien-I_Glixon_113-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-NB_OBrien-I_Glixon-113">[nb 5]</a></sup> was already described by Frederic A. Foss of [IBM](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IBM "IBM")<sup id="cite_ref-Foss_1954_1_114-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Foss_1954_1-114">[109]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Foss_1954_2_115-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Foss_1954_2-115">[110]</a></sup> and used by [Varec](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#Varec) in 1954. Later, it was also known as Watts code or Watts reflected decimal (WRD) code and is sometimes ambiguously referred to as reflected binary modified Gray code.<sup id="cite_ref-Evans_1958_116-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Evans_1958-116">[111]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Evans_1960_19-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Evans_1960-19">[19]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Evans_1961_20-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Evans_1961-20">[20]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Benjamin-Nicholls_1963_117-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Benjamin-Nicholls_1963-117">[112]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Klinkowski_1964_118-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Klinkowski_1964-118">[113]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Klinkowski_1966_119-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Klinkowski_1966-119">[114]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EDN_1967_120-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-EDN_1967-120">[115]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Toth-Zentai_1979_121-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Toth-Zentai_1979-121">[116]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Savard_2018_122-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Savard_2018-122">[117]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NB_Arithmetic_conversion_53-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-NB_Arithmetic_conversion-53">[nb 1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NB_Modified_96-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-NB_Modified-96">[nb 3]</a></sup> An O'Brien type-II code was already used by [Datex](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#Datex) in 1954.<sup id="cite_ref-NB_Petherick_OBrien-II_108-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-NB_Petherick_OBrien-II-108">[nb 4]</a></sup>)
-   Excess-3 Gray code (1956)<sup id="cite_ref-Turvey_1956_123-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Turvey_1956-123">[118]</a></sup> (aka Gray [excess-3](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Excess-3 "Excess-3") code,<sup id="cite_ref-Dokter-Steinhauer_1973_90-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Dokter-Steinhauer_1973-90">[88]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Dokter-Steinhauer_1975_91-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Dokter-Steinhauer_1975-91">[89]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MIL_1991_7-4"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-MIL_1991-7">[7]</a></sup> Gray 3-excess code, reflex excess-3 code, excess Gray code,<sup id="cite_ref-Hoklas_2005_1_103-3"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Hoklas_2005_1-103">[100]</a></sup> Gray excess code, 10-excess-3 Gray code or Gray–Stibitz code), described by Frank P. Turvey Jr. of [ITT](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Telephone_and_Telegraph_Corporation "International Telephone and Telegraph Corporation").<sup id="cite_ref-Turvey_1956_123-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Turvey_1956-123">[118]</a></sup>
-   Tompkins codes I and II (1956)<sup id="cite_ref-Tompkins_1956_3-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Tompkins_1956-3">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Steinbuch_1962_111-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Steinbuch_1962-111">[107]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Steinbuch-Weber-Heinemann_1974_112-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Steinbuch-Weber-Heinemann_1974-112">[108]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Dokter-Steinhauer_1973_90-3"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Dokter-Steinhauer_1973-90">[88]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Dokter-Steinhauer_1975_91-3"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Dokter-Steinhauer_1975-91">[89]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Hoklas_2005_1_103-4"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Hoklas_2005_1-103">[100]</a></sup>
-   Glixon code (1957), sometimes ambiguously also called modified Gray code<sup id="cite_ref-Glixon_1957_124-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Glixon_1957-124">[119]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Powell_1968_55-3"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Powell_1968-55">[54]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Borucki-Dittmann_1971_125-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Borucki-Dittmann_1971-125">[120]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Kämmerer_1969_126-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-K%C3%A4mmerer_1969-126">[121]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Steinbuch_1962_111-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Steinbuch_1962-111">[107]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Steinbuch-Weber-Heinemann_1974_112-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Steinbuch-Weber-Heinemann_1974-112">[108]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Dokter-Steinhauer_1973_90-4"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Dokter-Steinhauer_1973-90">[88]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Dokter-Steinhauer_1975_91-4"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Dokter-Steinhauer_1975-91">[89]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Hoklas_2005_1_103-5"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-Hoklas_2005_1-103">[100]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NB_Modified_96-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-NB_Modified-96">[nb 3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NB_OBrien-I_Glixon_113-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_note-NB_OBrien-I_Glixon-113">[nb 5]</a></sup>

## See also\[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Gray_code&action=edit&section=30 "Edit section: See also")\]

-   [Linear-feedback shift register](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Linear-feedback_shift_register "Linear-feedback shift register")
-   [De Bruijn sequence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/De_Bruijn_sequence "De Bruijn sequence")
-   [Steinhaus–Johnson–Trotter algorithm](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steinhaus%E2%80%93Johnson%E2%80%93Trotter_algorithm "Steinhaus–Johnson–Trotter algorithm") – an algorithm that generates Gray codes for the [factorial number system](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Factorial_number_system "Factorial number system")
-   [Minimum distance code](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decoding_methods#Minimum_distance_decoding "Decoding methods")
-   [Prouhet–Thue–Morse sequence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prouhet%E2%80%93Thue%E2%80%93Morse_sequence "Prouhet–Thue–Morse sequence") – related to inverse Gray code
-   [Ryser formula](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ryser_formula "Ryser formula")
-   [Hilbert curve](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hilbert_curve "Hilbert curve")

## Notes\[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Gray_code&action=edit&section=31 "Edit section: Notes")\]

1.  ^ [Jump up to: <sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup>](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_ref-NB_Arithmetic_conversion_53-0) [<sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup>](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_ref-NB_Arithmetic_conversion_53-1) [<sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup>](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_ref-NB_Arithmetic_conversion_53-2) By applying a simple _inversion rule_, the Gray code and the [O'Brien code I](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#O'Brien_I) can be translated into the 8421 [pure binary code](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pure_binary_code "Pure binary code") and the 2421 [Aiken code](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aiken_code "Aiken code"), respectively, to ease arithmetic operations.<sup><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#CITEREFEvans1961">[C]</a></sup>
2.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_ref-NB_OEIS_A007814_60-0 "Jump up")** Sequence 0, 1, 0, 2, 0, 1, 0, 3, … (sequence [A007814](https://oeis.org/A007814 "oeis:A007814") in the [OEIS](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/On-Line_Encyclopedia_of_Integer_Sequences "On-Line Encyclopedia of Integer Sequences")).
3.  ^ [Jump up to: <sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup>](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_ref-NB_Modified_96-0) [<sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup>](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_ref-NB_Modified_96-1) [<sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup>](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_ref-NB_Modified_96-2) There are several Gray code variants which are called "modified" of some sort: The [Glixon code](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#Glixon) is sometimes called modified Gray code.<sup><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#CITEREFPowell1968">[D]</a></sup> The [Lucal code](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#Lucal) is also called modified reflected binary code (MRB).<sup><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#CITEREFSellers,_Jr.HsiaoBearnson1968">[E]</a></sup> The [O'Brien code I](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#O'Brien_I) or Watts code is sometimes referred to as reflected binary modified Gray code.<sup><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#CITEREFSavard2018">[F]</a></sup>
4.  ^ [Jump up to: <sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup>](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_ref-NB_Petherick_OBrien-II_108-0) [<sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup>](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_ref-NB_Petherick_OBrien-II_108-1) [<sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup>](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_ref-NB_Petherick_OBrien-II_108-2) [<sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup>](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_ref-NB_Petherick_OBrien-II_108-3) By interchanging and inverting three bit rows, the [O'Brien code II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#O'Brien_II) and the [Petherick code](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#Petherick) can be transferred into each other.
5.  ^ [Jump up to: <sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup>](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_ref-NB_OBrien-I_Glixon_113-0) [<sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup>](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_ref-NB_OBrien-I_Glixon_113-1) [<sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup>](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_ref-NB_OBrien-I_Glixon_113-2) [<sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup>](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_ref-NB_OBrien-I_Glixon_113-3) By swapping two pairs of bit rows, individually shifting four bit rows and inverting one of them, the [Glixon code](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#Glixon) and the [O'Brien code I](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#O'Brien_I) can be transferred into each other.
6.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_ref-NB_Other_codes_127-0 "Jump up")** Other unit-distance BCD codes include the non-Gray code related 5-bit [Libaw–Craig](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Libaw%E2%80%93Craig_code "Libaw–Craig code") and the [1-2-1 code](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1-2-1_code "1-2-1 code").
7.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_ref-NB_Weights_128-0 "Jump up")** Depending on a code's target application, the [Hamming weights](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hamming_weight "Hamming weight") of a code can be important properties beyond coding-theoretical considerations also for physical reasons. Under some circumstances the all-cleared and/or all-set states must be omitted (f.e. to avoid non-conductive or short-circuit conditions), it may be desirable to keep the highest used weight as low as possible (f.e. to reduce power consumption of the reader circuit) or to keep the variance of used weights small (f.e. to reduce acoustic noise or current fluctuations).
8.  ^ [Jump up to: <sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup>](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_ref-NB_Tracks_Inverse_129-0) [<sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup>](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_ref-NB_Tracks_Inverse_129-1) [<sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup>](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_ref-NB_Tracks_Inverse_129-2) For [Gray BCD](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#Gray_BCD), [Paul](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#Paul) and [Klar codes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#Klar), the number of necessary reading tracks can be reduced from 4 to 3 if inversion of one of the middle tracks is acceptable.
9.  ^ [Jump up to: <sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup>](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_ref-NB_Complement_InvertTop_131-0) [<sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup>](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_ref-NB_Complement_InvertTop_131-1) [<sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup>](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_ref-NB_Complement_InvertTop_131-2) [<sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup>](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_ref-NB_Complement_InvertTop_131-3) [<sup><i><b>e</b></i></sup>](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_ref-NB_Complement_InvertTop_131-4) [<sup><i><b>f</b></i></sup>](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_ref-NB_Complement_InvertTop_131-5) For [O'Brien codes I](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#O'Brien_I) and [II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#O'Brien_II) and [Petherick](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#Petherick), [Susskind](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#Susskind), [Klar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#Klar) as well as [Excess-3 Gray codes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#Gray_excess), a [9s complement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/9s_complement "9s complement") can be derived by inverting the most-significant (fourth) binary digit.
10.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_ref-NB_Complement_Tompkins_134-0 "Jump up")** For [Tompkins code II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#Tompkins_II), a [9s complement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/9s_complement "9s complement") can be derived by inverting the first three digits and swapping the two middle binary digits.

New York, USA: [Technology Press of the Massachusetts Institute of Technology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Technology_Press_of_the_Massachusetts_Institute_of_Technology "Technology Press of the Massachusetts Institute of Technology") / [John Wiley & Sons, Inc.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Wiley_%26_Sons,_Inc. The contents of the book was originally prepared by staff members of the [Servomechanisms Laboraratory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MIT_Servomechanisms_Laboratory "MIT Servomechanisms Laboratory"), Department of Electrical Engineering, [MIT](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Massachusetts_Institute_of_Technology "Massachusetts Institute of Technology"), for Special Summer Programs held in 1956 and 1957. Susskind's "reading-type code" is actually a minor variant of the code shown here with the two most significant bit rows swapped to better illustrate symmetries. Also, by swapping two bit rows and inverting one of them, the code can be transferred into the [Petherick code](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#Petherick), whereas by swapping and inverting two bit rows, the code can be transferred into the [O'Brien code II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#O'Brien_II).)

11.  ^ [Jump up to: <sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup>](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_ref-Winder_1959_11-0) [<sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup>](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_ref-Winder_1959_11-1) [<sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup>](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_ref-Winder_1959_11-2) [<sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup>](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_ref-Winder_1959_11-3) [<sup><i><b>e</b></i></sup>](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_ref-Winder_1959_11-4) Winder, C. Farrell (October 1959). ["Shaft Angle Encoders Afford High Accuracy"](https://web.archive.org/web/20200928132232/https://worldradiohistory.com/Archive-Tele-Tech/50s/Electronic-Industries-1959-10.pdf) (PDF). _[Electronic Industries](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electronic_Industries_(journal) "Electronic Industries (journal)")_. [Chilton Company](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chilton_Company "Chilton Company"). **18** (10): 76–80. Archived from [the original](https://worldradiohistory.com/Archive-Tele-Tech/50s/Electronic-Industries-1959-10.pdf) (PDF) on 2020-09-28. Retrieved 2018-01-14. p. 78: \[…\] The type of code wheel most popular in [optical encoders](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Optical_encoder "Optical encoder") contains a cyclic binary code pattern designed to give a cyclic sequence of "on-off" outputs. The cyclic binary code is also known as the cyclic progression code, the reflected binary code, and the Gray code. This code was originated by [G. R. Stibitz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/G._R._Stibitz "G. R. Stibitz"), of [Bell Telephone Laboratories](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bell_Telephone_Laboratories "Bell Telephone Laboratories"), and was first proposed for [pulse-code modulation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pulse-code_modulation "Pulse-code modulation") systems by [Frank Gray](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frank_Gray_(researcher) "Frank Gray (researcher)"), also of BTL. Thus the name Gray code. The Gray or cyclic code is used mainly to eliminate the possibility of errors at code transition which could result in gross ambiguities. \[…\]

19.  ^ [Jump up to: <sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup>](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_ref-Evans_1960_19-0) [<sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup>](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_ref-Evans_1960_19-1) Evans, David Silvester (1960). 20.  ^ [Jump up to: <sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup>](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_ref-Evans_1961_20-0) [<sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup>](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_ref-Evans_1961_20-1) Evans, David Silvester (March 1961). "Chapter Three: Direct Reading from Coded Scales". [_Digital Data: Their derivation and reduction for analysis and process control_](https://books.google.com/books?id=WOIJAAAAMAAJ) (1 ed.). London, UK: [Hilger & Watts Ltd](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hilger_%26_Watts_Ltd "Hilger & Watts Ltd") / [Interscience Publishers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interscience_Publishers "Interscience Publishers"). pp. 18–23. Retrieved 2020-05-24. p. 20–23: \[…\] Decoding. \[…\] To decode C.P.B. or [W.R.D.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#Watts) codes, a simple inversion rule can be applied. The readings of the higher tracks determine the way in which the lower tracks are translated. The inversion rule is applied line by line for the C.P.B. and for the W.R.D. it is applied decade by decade or line by line. Starting therefore with the top or slowest changing track of the C.P.B., if the result is odd (1) the next track value has to be inverted, i.e. 0 for 1 and 1 for 0. If, however, the first track is even (0), the second track is left as read, i.e. 0 for 0 and 1 for 1. Again, if the resultant reading of the second track is odd, the third track reading is inverted and so on. When an odd is changed to an even the line below is not inverted and when an even is changed to an odd the line below is inverted. The result of applying this rule to the pattern \[…\] is the [pure binary](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pure_binary_code "Pure binary code") (P.B.) pattern \[…\] where each track or digit can be given a definite numerical value (in this instance 1, 2, 4, 8, etc.). \[…\] Using the line-by-line inversion rule on the W.R.D. code produces \[a\] pattern \[of [1, 2, 4, 2 code](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aiken_code "Aiken code")\] where again the digits can be given numerical values and summed decade by decade. The summing of the digits can be very useful, for example, in a high-speed scanning system; but in a parallel decoding system \[…\], it is usual to treat each binary quartet or decade as an entity. In other words, if the first or more significant decade is odd, the second decade is rectified or complemented by inverting the D track and so on, the result being the repeating pattern of \[rectified W.R.D. code\]. This is an extremely easy thing to achieve since the only change required is the inversion of the meaning of the D track or complementing digit. \[…\] (8+82 pages) (NB. The author does not mention Gray at all and calls the standard Gray code "Cyclic Permuted Binary Code" (C.P.B.), the book index erroneously lists it as "cyclic pure binary code".)

When I first heard the name I took it as referring to [Elisha Gray](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elisha_Gray "Elisha Gray"), and [Heath](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#CITEREFHeath1961) testifies to his usage of it. 34.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_ref-Fischer_2000_34-0 "Jump up")** Fischer, Eric N. (2000-06-20). ["The Evolution of Character Codes, 1874–1968"](https://archive.org/details/enf-ascii). ark:/13960/t07x23w8s. Retrieved 2020-12-20. \[…\] In 1872, \[Baudot\] started research toward a telegraph system that would allow multiple operators to transmit simultaneously over a single wire and, as the transmissions were received, would print them in ordinary alphabetic characters on a strip of paper. He received a patent for such a system on June 17, 1874. \[…\] Instead of a variable delay followed by a single-unit pulse, Baudot's system used a uniform six time units to transmit each character. \[…\] his early telegraph probably used the six-unit code \[…\] that he attributes to [Davy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edward_Davy "Edward Davy") in an 1877 article. \[…\] in 1876 Baudot redesigned his equipment to use a five-unit code. Punctuation and digits were still sometimes needed, though, so he adopted from [Hughes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_Edward_Hughes "David Edward Hughes") the use of two special letter space and figure space characters that would cause the printer to shift between cases at the same time as it advanced the paper without printing. The five-unit code he began using at this time \[…\] was structured to suit his keyboard \[…\], which controlled two units of each character with switches operated by the left hand and the other three units with the right hand. \[…\] [\[5\]](https://web.archive.org/web/20180919020435/http://index-of.es/Varios-2/ASCII%20The%20Evolution%20of%20Character%20Codes.pdf)[\[6\]](https://archive.org/details/enf-ascii)

42.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_ref-Zemanek_1976_42-0 "Jump up")** [Zemanek, Heinrich "Heinz" Josef](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heinrich_Josef_Zemanek "Heinrich Josef Zemanek") (1976-06-07). ["Computer prehistory and history in central Europe"](https://www.computer.org/csdl/pds/api/csdl/proceedings/download-article/12OmNzZEAtH/pdf). Written at Vienna, Austria. _International Workshop on Managing Requirements Knowledge_. AFIPS '76: Proceedings of the June 7–10, 1976, national computer conference and exposition June 1976. Vol. 1. New York, USA: [American Federation of Information Processing Societies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Federation_of_Information_Processing_Societies "American Federation of Information Processing Societies"), [Association for Computing Machinery](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Association_for_Computing_Machinery "Association for Computing Machinery"). pp. 15–20. [doi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Doi_(identifier) "Doi (identifier)"):[10.1145/1499799.1499803](https://doi.org/10.1145%2F1499799.1499803). [ISBN](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ISBN_(identifier) "ISBN (identifier)") [978-1-4503-7917-5](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-1-4503-7917-5 "Special:BookSources/978-1-4503-7917-5"). [S2CID](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/S2CID_(identifier) "S2CID (identifier)") [14114959](https://api.semanticscholar.org/CorpusID:14114959). [Archived](https://web.archive.org/web/20201217230013/https://www.computer.org/csdl/pds/api/csdl/proceedings/download-article/12OmNzZEAtH/pdf) from the original on 2020-12-17. Retrieved 2020-12-17. p. 17: \[…\] In 1874, [Schaeffler](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Otto_Sch%C3%A4ffler&action=edit&redlink=1 "Otto Schäffler (page does not exist)") \[[de](https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theodor_Heinrich_Otto_Sch%C3%A4ffler "de:Theodor Heinrich Otto Schäffler")\] invented another [printing telegraph](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Printing_telegraph "Printing telegraph"), a quadruple system like the [Baudot](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baudot_telegraph "Baudot telegraph"), but mechanically more sophisticated. The [Hughes telegraph](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hughes_telegraph "Hughes telegraph") had two synchronously rotating fingers, one in the sender and one in the receiver. By a piano-like keyboard the operator selected a letter and thereby made contact with the rotating finger in the corresponding direction. Since the receiving finger was in the same direction at this moment, the receiver could print the correct letter. The Baudot and the Schaeffler printing telegraphs use a five-bit binary code. ... Schaeffler's code is a reflected binary code! What [F. Gray](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frank_Gray_(researcher) "Frank Gray (researcher)") patented in 1953 for [PCM](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/PCM "PCM"), Schaeffler had applied in his telegraph in 1874, and for a similar reason: reliability. He had contact fingers sensing on five cams consecutively all combinations; the right one triggers printing. If the fingers are to make a minimal number of movements, the solution is the reflected binary code. For Schaeffler, this idea was a minor one. More exactly, the code is described in a letter by the Austrian Post employee, J\[ohann\] N\[epomuk\] Teufelhart, [inserted there](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#CITEREFRothen1878) as a footnote and telling that Schaeffler found the code by combining wooden bars with the different combinations until he had the best solution. Another Post employee, Alexander Wilhelm Lambert of Linz, claims to have shown this code to Schaeffler as early as 1872, but this claim is not clear and cannot be checked. \[…\] (6 pages)

46.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_ref-Brown_2012_46-0 "Jump up")** Brown, Frank Markham (2012) \[2003, 1990\]. Retrieved 2020-05-11. p. 53: \[…\] The [Datex code](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#Datex) \[…\] uses the [O'Brien code II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#O'Brien_II) within each decade, and reflected decimal numbers for the decimal transitions. For further processing, code conversion to the natural decimal notation is necessary. Since the O'Brien II code forms a [9s complement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/9s_complement "9s complement"), this does not give rise to particular difficulties: whenever the code word for the tens represents an odd number, the code words for the decimal units are given as the 9s complements by inversion of the fourth binary digit. \[…\] (270 pages)

103.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_ref-Baumgartner_1963_106-0 "Jump up")** ["Digitizer als Analog-Digital-Wandler in der Steuer-, Meß- und Regeltechnik"](https://web.archive.org/web/20200521211656/https://www.posital.com/media/posital_media/documents/TechnischeMitteilung_May1963.pdf) (PDF). _Technische Mitteilungen_. Relais, elektronische Geräte, Steuerungen (in German). No. 13. Cologne-Niehl, Germany: Franz Baumgartner (FraBa). May 1963. pp. 1–2. Archived from [the original](https://www.posital.com/media/posital_media/documents/TechnischeMitteilung_May1963.pdf) (PDF) on 2020-05-21. Retrieved 2020-05-21. pp. 1–2: \[…\] Die Firma Harrison Reproduction Equipment, Farnborough/England \[…\] hat in jahrelanger Entwicklung in Zusammenarbeit mit der Britischen Luftwaffe und britischen Industriebetrieben den mechanischen Digitizer \[…\] zu einer technischen Reife gebracht, die fast allen Anforderungen \[…\] genügt. \[…\] Um bei der dezimalen Entschlüsselung des verwendeten Binärcodes zu eindeutigen und bei der Übergabe von einer Dezimalstelle zur anderen in der Reihenfolge immer richtigen Ergebnissen zu kommen, wurde ein spezieller Code entwickelt, der jede Möglichkeit einer Fehlaussage durch sein Prinzip ausschließt und der außerdem durch seinen Aufbau eine relativ einfache Entschlüsselung erlaubt. Der Code basiert auf dem [Petherick-Code](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#Petherick). \[…\] (4 pages)

[ISBN](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ISBN_(identifier) "ISBN (identifier)") [978-3-642-80561-5](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-3-642-80561-5 "Special:BookSources/978-3-642-80561-5"). (viii+252 pages) [1st edition](https://books.google.com/books?id=NwyCBwAAQBAJ&pg=PA15) (NB. Like [Kämmerer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#CITEREFK%C3%A4mmerer1969), the authors describe a 6-bit 20-cyclic Glixon code.)
121.  ^ [Jump up to: <sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup>](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_ref-K%C3%A4mmerer_1969_126-0) [<sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup>](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_ref-K%C3%A4mmerer_1969_126-1) [Kämmerer, Wilhelm](https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wilhelm_K%C3%A4mmerer "de:Wilhelm Kämmerer") \[in German\] (May 1969). "II.15. Struktur: Informationsdarstellung im Automaten". Written at Jena, Germany. In [Frühauf, Hans](https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hans_Fr%C3%BChauf "de:Hans Frühauf") \[in German\]; Kämmerer, Wilhelm; Schröder, Kurz; Winkler, Helmut (eds.). _Digitale Automaten – Theorie, Struktur, Technik, Programmieren_. Elektronisches Rechnen und Regeln (in German). Vol. 5 (1 ed.). Berlin, Germany: [Akademie-Verlag GmbH](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Akademie-Verlag_GmbH "Akademie-Verlag GmbH"). p. 173. License no. 202-100/416/69. Order no. 4666 ES 20 K 3. (NB. A second edition 1973 exists as well. Like [Borucki and Dittmann](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#CITEREFBoruckiDittmann1971), but without naming it Glixon code, the author creates a 20-cyclic tetradic code from Glixon code and a Glixon code variant with inverted high-order bit.)
122.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_ref-Paul_1995_130-0 "Jump up")** Paul, Matthias R. (1995-08-10) \[1994\]. ["Unterbrechungsfreier Schleifencode"](http://www.uni-bonn.de/~uzs180/download/mpbcd102.zip) \[Continuous loop code\]. 1.02 (in German). Retrieved 2008-02-11. (NB. The author called this code _Schleifencode_ (English: "loop code"). It differs from Gray BCD code only in the encoding of state 0 to make it a cyclic unit-distance code for full-circle rotatory applications. Avoiding the all-zero code pattern allows for loop self-testing and to use the data lines for uninterrupted power distribution.)
123.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_ref-Klar_1970_132-0 "Jump up")** Klar, Rainer (1970-02-01). [_Digitale Rechenautomaten – Eine Einführung_](https://books.google.com/books?id=QnqVDwAAQBAJ&pg=PA17) \[_Digital Computers – An Introduction_\]. Sammlung Göschen (in German). Vol. 1241/1241a (1 ed.). Berlin, Germany: [Walter de Gruyter & Co.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Walter_de_Gruyter_%26_Co. "Walter de Gruyter & Co.") / [G. J. Göschen'sche Verlagsbuchhandlung](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/G._J._G%C3%B6schen%27sche_Verlagsbuchhandlung "G. J. Göschen'sche Verlagsbuchhandlung") \[[de](https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/G._J._G%C3%B6schen%27sche_Verlagsbuchhandlung "de:G. J. Göschen'sche Verlagsbuchhandlung")\]. p. 17. [ISBN](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ISBN_(identifier) "ISBN (identifier)") [3-11-083160-0](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special:BookSources/3-11-083160-0 "Special:BookSources/3-11-083160-0"). . Archiv-Nr. 7990709. [Archived](https://web.archive.org/web/20200601100645/https://books.google.de/books?id=QnqVDwAAQBAJ&pg=PA17&lpg=PA17&redir_esc=y) from the original on 2020-06-01. Retrieved 2020-04-13. (205 pages) (NB. A 2019 reprint of the first edition is available under [ISBN](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ISBN_(identifier) "ISBN (identifier)") [3-11002793-3](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special:BookSources/3-11002793-3 "Special:BookSources/3-11002793-3"), [978-3-11002793-8](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-3-11002793-8 "Special:BookSources/978-3-11002793-8"). A reworked and expanded [4th edition](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#CITEREFKlar1989) exists as well.)
124.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#cite_ref-Klar_1989_133-0 "Jump up")** Klar, Rainer (1989) \[1988-10-01\]. _Digitale Rechenautomaten – Eine Einführung in die Struktur von Computerhardware_ \[_Digital Computers – An Introduction into the structure of computer hardware_\]. Sammlung Göschen (in German). Vol. 2050 (4th reworked ed.). Berlin, Germany: [Walter de Gruyter & Co.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Walter_de_Gruyter_%26_Co. "Walter de Gruyter & Co.") p. 28. [ISBN](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ISBN_(identifier) "ISBN (identifier)") [3-11011700-2](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special:BookSources/3-11011700-2 "Special:BookSources/3-11011700-2"). (320 pages) (NB. The author called this code _Einheitsabstandscode_ (English: "unit-distance code"). By swapping two bit rows and inverting one of them, it can be transferred into the [O'Brien code II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#O'Brien_II), whereas by swapping and inverting two bit rows, it can be transferred into the [Petherick code](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gray_code#Petherick).)

## External links\[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Gray_code&action=edit&section=34 "Edit section: External links")\]

-   ["Gray Code" demonstration](http://demonstrations.wolfram.com/BinaryGrayCode/) by Michael Schreiber, [Wolfram Demonstrations Project](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wolfram_Demonstrations_Project "Wolfram Demonstrations Project") (with Mathematica implementation). 2007.
-   [NIST Dictionary of Algorithms and Data Structures: Gray code](https://xlinux.nist.gov/dads/HTML/graycode.html).
-   [Hitch Hiker's Guide to Evolutionary Computation, Q21: What are Gray codes, and why are they used?](https://web.archive.org/web/20151026021510/http://www.aip.de/~ast/EvolCompFAQ/Q21.htm), including [C](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/C_(programming_language) "C (programming language)") code to convert between binary and BRGC.
-   Dragos A. Harabor uses [Gray codes in a 3D digitizer](https://web.archive.org/web/20151122120754/http://www.ugcs.caltech.edu/~dragos/3DP/coord.html).
-   Single-track gray codes, binary [chain codes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chain_code "Chain code") ([Lancaster 1994](http://tinaja.com/text/chain01.html)), and [linear-feedback shift registers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Linear-feedback_shift_register "Linear-feedback shift register") are all useful in finding one's absolute position on a single-track rotary encoder (or other position sensor).
-   [AMS Column: Gray codes](https://www.ams.org/featurecolumn/archive/gray.html)
-   [Optical Encoder Wheel Generator](http://www.bushytails.net/~randyg/encoder/encoderwheel.html)
-   [ProtoTalk.net – Understanding Quadrature Encoding](https://web.archive.org/web/20110724021700/http://prototalk.net/forums/showthread.php?t=78) – Covers quadrature encoding in more detail with a focus on robotic applications
